                  <form>

                  </form>, originally <foreign lang="ar">تَوَبُوتٌ</foreign>, the <foreign lang="ar">ت</foreign> not being the characteristic of the fem. gender, (Z, MF, TA,) of the measure <foreign lang="ar">فَعَلُوتٌ</foreign>, and meaning <hi rend="ital">A chest,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">box,</hi> from <foreign lang="ar">التَّوْبُ</foreign>, because what is taken out from it continually returns to it: (AAF, IJ, Z, MF, TA:) or originally <foreign lang="ar">تَابُوَةٌ</foreign>; (S, K; [in the CK <foreign lang="ar">تَأْبُوَةٌ</foreign>;]) the <foreign lang="ar">و</foreign> being made quiescent, and the <foreign lang="ar">ة</foreign> changed into <foreign lang="ar">ت</foreign>: (S, K:) [in Chald. <H>?</H>: in Hebr. <H>?</H>:] it signifies also the <hi rend="ital">ribs, with what they contain, as the heart and the liver &amp;c.;</hi> as being likened to a chest, or box; (IAth, TA in art. <foreign lang="ar">تبت</foreign>;) the <hi rend="ital">chest, breast,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">bosom:</hi> (A in that art.:) or [primarily] the <hi rend="ital">ribs, with what they contain, as the heart &amp;c.:</hi> and [hence] applied to <hi rend="ital">a chest,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">box:</hi> (Towsheeh, MF, TA:) also written <foreign lang="ar">تَبُوتٌ</foreign>. (K in art. <foreign lang="ar">تبت</foreign>.) [It is generally applied in the present day to <hi rend="ital">a bier: a coffin:</hi> and <hi rend="ital">an oblong case that is placed over a grave:</hi> the pl. is <foreign lang="ar">تَوَابِيتُ</foreign>.] El-Kásim Ibn-Maan says that it is the only word in the Kur-án in respect of which the dialects of Kureysh and the Ansár differ; the former pronouncing it <foreign lang="ar">تَابُوتٌ</foreign>; (S;) and the latter, <foreign lang="ar">تَابُوهٌ</foreign>. (S, K.) But IB denies that its last letter is originally <foreign lang="ar">ة</foreign>, the fem. termination; asserting the final <foreign lang="ar">ت</foreign> to be a radical letter, the measure of the word to be <foreign lang="ar">فَاعُولٌ</foreign>, and its proper place in art. <foreign lang="ar">تبت</foreign>: he says that the final <foreign lang="ar">ت</foreign> is changed in a case of pause, but not generally, into <foreign lang="ar">ه</foreign>, as is that of <foreign lang="ar">الفُرَات</foreign> [the Euphrates], in which the <foreign lang="ar">ت</foreign> is not the fem. termination. (L, TA.)
